    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_241831194">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241831194" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="left imgcol" title="Kathryn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1320032014p2/4181111.jpg" alt="Kathryn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/241831194?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 01, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="user" title="Kathryn">Kathryn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6414515-the-foundling" title="Paperback 9781402219481" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4181111-kathryn?shelf=regency-romance" class="actionLinkLite">regency-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4181111-kathryn?shelf=2012-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer241831194">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12735907487448931833">I'm normally quite chary of stars, and don't award full marks to anything that isn't objectively good. So, in my reviews, four stars and below are subjective, while five stars are reserved for the best of the best. I've made one exception for <a title="Frederica by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311196.Frederica">Frederica</a>, and I find myself forced to make another for <em>The Foundling</em>.<br /><br /><em>The Foundling</em> tells the story of the Duke of Ware, a shy, retiring boy of twenty-four who has been cosseted and coddled until he could scream. But he's so mild-mannered that he merely sub</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12735907487448931833">I'm normally quite chary of stars, and don't award full marks to anything that isn't objectively good. So, in my reviews, four stars and below are subjective, while five stars are reserved for the best of the best. I've made one exception for <a title="Frederica by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311196.Frederica">Frederica</a>, and I find myself forced to make another for <em>The Foundling</em>.<br /><br /><em>The Foundling</em> tells the story of the Duke of Ware, a shy, retiring boy of twenty-four who has been cosseted and coddled until he could scream. But he's so mild-mannered that he merely submits; he can't bear to hurt the feelings of his faithful retainers. Finally, however, he decides to break free, and the titular foundling is the impetus for much of his adventures.<br /><br />This book is rather unusual for a Heyer book in that the viewpoint character is male (we do get Harriet's point of view a few times, but Gilly, the Duke, is the viewpoint character for the majority of the book) and the romance is understated. (It's there, though. I can see why some readers would think it's underdeveloped, but the interactions between Gilly and Harriet show a genuine respect and affection for one another.) It's more of a coming of age book than a romance. Also, Gilly isn't a typical Heyer hero. His cousin Gideon is, right down to the saturnine aspect, but Gilly is much more mild-mannered; he's not the usual cynical, assured gentleman who is slap up to the echo in every respect. Gilly is an expert marksman, but otherwise, he doesn't care for the usual pursuits of a Regency gentleman.<br /><br />In other ways, however, <em>The Foundling</em> has many of the stock attributes of Heyer romances, including the convoluted plot and the grandmother from a decidedly less prim generation who has no patience for missishness. It also features Mr Liversedge, a plausible rogue who kept me in stitches with every appearance, and Tom, an impetuous young boy who gets Gilly mixed up in his adventures. In fact, once the plot really gets going, the whole book is hilarious. <br /><br />I love this book for the humor and the characters, and I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12735907487448931833">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_286659134">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286659134" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5780390-mostlydelores" class="left imgcol" title="MostlyDelores"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1392122618p2/5780390.jpg" alt="MostlyDelores" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/286659134?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5780390-mostlydelores" class="user" title="MostlyDelores">MostlyDelores</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7417665-the-foundling" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5780390-mostlydelores?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5780390-mostlydelores?shelf=excellent" class="actionLinkLite">excellent</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5780390-mostlydelores?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer286659134">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7570493839732270556">This is a romance only in the sense that the hero is happily settled with his lady at the end of the book; really it is an adventure and, I suppose, a journey of self-discovery, although I'm sure Georgette Heyer would never use (or approve of) such a navel-gazing term. <br /><br />In his travels, Gilly encounters Tom, a magnet for mischief of all kinds, Belinda, a beautiful, empty-headed girl whose virtue is teetering on a knife-edge, a brace of villains, and a host of citizens of all stripes that, as a Duk</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7570493839732270556">This is a romance only in the sense that the hero is happily settled with his lady at the end of the book; really it is an adventure and, I suppose, a journey of self-discovery, although I'm sure Georgette Heyer would never use (or approve of) such a navel-gazing term. <br /><br />In his travels, Gilly encounters Tom, a magnet for mischief of all kinds, Belinda, a beautiful, empty-headed girl whose virtue is teetering on a knife-edge, a brace of villains, and a host of citizens of all stripes that, as a Duke, he had never had to deal with before.<br /><br />I love sweet-tempered Gilly, another of Heyer's non-standard heroes, his friendship with his cousin Gideon, and his irascible Uncle Lionel. And, as usual with Heyer, the language is delightful. <br /><br />The first course:<br /><em>Lord Lionel being an advocate of what he considered a neat, plain dinner, only two courses were served at Sale Park when the family dined alone. The first of these consisted of a tureen of turtle, removed with fish, which was in its turn removed with a haunch of venison. Several side-dishes, such as pork cutlets with Rober sauce, larded fillets of beef, tenderones of veal and truffles, and a braised ham, graced the board...</em><br /><br />The Duke to his retinue:<br /><em>"I daresay I could have been tolerably comfortable without a Chief Confectioner."<br />Everyone realized that the Duke had uttered a witticism, so those whose social status permitted them to laugh, did so, in a discreet way; and Mr. Scriven said that he hoped his Grace would not find his house to be quite so ill-prepared as that.</em> <br /><br />Gilly's valet and Gideon's manservant:<br /><em>"You looby, if you don't stand out of my way you'll get one in the bread basket as'll send you to grass!" said Nettlebed fiercely.<br />"Ho!" retorted Wragby, "Ho, I will, will I?" If it's a bit of home-brewed you're wanting, you herring-gutted, blubber-headed chinch, put up your mawleys!"</em><br /><br />Sir Timothy:<br /><em> "I do feel that a little openess in dear Gideon--a little less reserve--would be wise at this delicate moment! He has not been--how shall I put it?--precisely conciliating, one feels."</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7570493839732270556">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4437356144225777062">This is really more a coming of age novel than a romance; there is a romance, of course, but it takes a distant second place to Heyer's account of how her hero, Gilly, Duke of Sale, goes adventuring, in a smartly paced plot, and frees himself from the confinement of his family and his title. The romance wasn't much (and I actually found Gilly's romantic interest rather dull), but the friendship between Gilly and his dashing cousin, Gideon, was a highlight of the book. I don't think I've read a H</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4437356144225777062">This is really more a coming of age novel than a romance; there is a romance, of course, but it takes a distant second place to Heyer's account of how her hero, Gilly, Duke of Sale, goes adventuring, in a smartly paced plot, and frees himself from the confinement of his family and his title. The romance wasn't much (and I actually found Gilly's romantic interest rather dull), but the friendship between Gilly and his dashing cousin, Gideon, was a highlight of the book. I don't think I've read a Heyer before in which a friendship between two men was such a focus, and I liked it quite a bit. </span>

              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=5-star-historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">5-star-historical-romance</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer2046419335570856472">4  stars. Wonderful story. Problem with audiobook narrator’s breaths.<br /><br />I think my favorite trope is seeing a character change - like this. Gilly was small, skinny, shy, quiet, and obedient - doing whatever his overbearing uncle and others told him to do. Even with marriage the uncle says it’s time you get engaged to Harriet, so he does. He’s 24. Gilly decides to go on a journey alone without his valet or other hired help. On that journey things happen that allow Gilly to act differently and to see</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2046419335570856472">4 ½ stars. Wonderful story. Problem with audiobook narrator’s breaths.<br /><br />I think my favorite trope is seeing a character change - like this. Gilly was small, skinny, shy, quiet, and obedient - doing whatever his overbearing uncle and others told him to do. Even with marriage the uncle says it’s time you get engaged to Harriet, so he does. He’s 24. Gilly decides to go on a journey alone without his valet or other hired help. On that journey things happen that allow Gilly to act differently and to see himself differently than he had before. I was delighted and surprised. And there were humorous parts. It’s a little slow to start. But the last third was fulfilling.<br /><br />This is not typical romance, but it has a happy romantic ending. This is primarily Gilly’s coming of age story. The heroine has a small role.<br /><br />A minor complaint for the author. She called characters by different names, sometimes the first name, sometimes the last name. I was confused about the two Wares and then Gideon and Gaywood sounding similar. Gideon Ware (the son of Lord Lionel) was also called Captain Gideon or Captain Ware. Mathew Ware (the son of Lord Henry Ware). Charles Presteigne (Harriet’s brother) was called Charles, Charlie, and Gaywood. Now that I’ve looked them up after reading the book, they don’t seem as confusing. But at the time I was confused.<br /><br />AUDIOBOOK NARRATOR - Phyllida Nash.<br />Her breaths were annoying and distracting. When talking to someone in person one does not hear breaths. Parts of the story were ok, but several times I was thinking when is the next breath going to come? They interrupted the story. Narrators: PLEASE listen to the recording of yourself and if you hear your breaths, use a different microphone - or stand farther away from it.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 3rd person. Unabridged audiobook length: 14 hrs and 26 mins. Swearing language: none. Sexual content: none. Setting: 1818 England. Book copyright: 1948. Genre: historical fiction with romance.<br /><br />OTHER BOOKS by Georgette Heyer:<br />My favorite books are: These Old Shades, Cotillion, and Friday’s Child. My second favorites: Devil’s Cub, Lady of Quality, The Convenient Marriage, and A Civil Contract.</span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3727861-andrea?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3727861-andrea?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3727861-andrea?shelf=1800s" class="actionLinkLite">1800s</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1328823215">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7267401280408951710">This is more adventure than romance, and bears a strong resemblance to <a title="Charity Girl by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311218.Charity_Girl">Charity Girl</a>, with another 'unsuitable' female in need of rescue, and handed over to a long-standing friend-come-love interest of the main male character. But most of the story is caught up in the adventures of Gilly as he kicks over the traces and goes on a mission of mercy (and meets another 'Falstaff' type, though this one theoretically intended to be more amusing).<br /><br />The story works a little better than Charity Girl, but it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7267401280408951710">This is more adventure than romance, and bears a strong resemblance to <a title="Charity Girl by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311218.Charity_Girl">Charity Girl</a>, with another 'unsuitable' female in need of rescue, and handed over to a long-standing friend-come-love interest of the main male character. But most of the story is caught up in the adventures of Gilly as he kicks over the traces and goes on a mission of mercy (and meets another 'Falstaff' type, though this one theoretically intended to be more amusing).<br /><br />The story works a little better than Charity Girl, but it is still full of rather too much of the things Gilly is trying to escape, which is hard to endure in a book, let alone a whole life.<br /><br />There are a few bright points, though - particularly the farmer's mother observing that Belinda's lack of morals is probably due to being a by-blow of the gentry. And Gideon and Gilly's friendship is nice.<br /><br />Even so, watching Gilly chafe against all the coddling restrictions placed upon him and finally begin to assert himself left me with a reflection that those restrictions are perhaps only a quarter so tight as those placed on poor Harriet, which dims my sympathy for him a trifle - particularly when it's suggested that his new-found pleasure in Harriet is owed to her tendency to do whatever he tells her to.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2070455107913546659">Sometimes rereads are A Very Good Thing.<br /><br />I was very young when I originally read this &amp; I didn't much care for it. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_76516850">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76516850" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" title="Wealhtheow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" alt="Wealhtheow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/76516850?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="user" title="Wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer76516850">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7907407917901636439">Gilly was born an incredibly rich duke. Far from trying to get his inheritance, his family did everything in its power to ensure that the sickly little boy would grow to manhood. However, now that Gilly's nearly of-age, their coddling and controlling is less welcome. Being pushed into an engagement with an old friend is the last straw, and Gilly takes an opportunity to flee his hangers-on and pretend to be just a gentleman. While doing so he rescues a fair but dimwitted maiden, takes on the char</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7907407917901636439">Gilly was born an incredibly rich duke. Far from trying to get his inheritance, his family did everything in its power to ensure that the sickly little boy would grow to manhood. However, now that Gilly's nearly of-age, their coddling and controlling is less welcome. Being pushed into an engagement with an old friend is the last straw, and Gilly takes an opportunity to flee his hangers-on and pretend to be just a gentleman. While doing so he rescues a fair but dimwitted maiden, takes on the charge of an adventurous boy, thumps villains on their heads, gets kidnapped, burns down a house, and all in all leads a very enterprising life indeed. <br /><br />I liked this book a great deal. It's largely free of Heyer's love of Regency-era slang, and the main character is far from her usual tall-saturnine-sardonic-controlling hero. The only issue I had was that the love between Gilly and the woman he ends up marrying seems to come out of nowhere. It's a regency romance, Heyer, you've got to put *some* effort into the romance part, no matter how meticulously researched the "regency" part is.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7907407917901636439">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1491953571">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1491953571" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4612196-tiffany-reisz" class="left imgcol" title="Tiffany Reisz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442527387p2/4612196.jpg" alt="Tiffany Reisz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1491953571?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 05, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4612196-tiffany-reisz" class="user" title="Tiffany Reisz">Tiffany Reisz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1491953571">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3440663597133035962">This book was adorable. Just adorable. I was so proud of Gilly. Heyer paints a wonderful sweet and believable portrait of a young man treated like a child all his life and yet still finds he has the heart of a man, and a good man too. My only complaint was that it dragged a bit. Could have been 50 pages shorter and I would have liked more scenes with the lovely Lady Harriet, but all in all, a wonderful read. </span>

          </span>

      <span id="like_container_review_1491953571" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/1491953571?resource_type=Review" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_review_1491953571"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F32111.The_Foundling" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/1491953571?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_672310386">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/672310386" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7217945-christopher" class="left imgcol" title="Christopher"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Christopher" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/672310386?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7217945-christopher" class="user" title="Christopher">Christopher</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7217945-christopher?shelf=clean" class="actionLinkLite">clean</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer672310386">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5113429021549445102">10/21/15<br />Upon rereading, I am convinced “The Foundling” is among Heyer’s best novels. It has a slow start, but by the middle of the story becomes an all-out adventure story that I couldn’t put down. It is an extremely original and well thought out coming of age story: mild-mannered protagonists, charming would-be murderers, various miscreants which the hero takes under his wing. As the reader, you look back once you’re well into the story and see how everything ties together – It’s something I ve</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5113429021549445102">10/21/15<br />Upon rereading, I am convinced “The Foundling” is among Heyer’s best novels. It has a slow start, but by the middle of the story becomes an all-out adventure story that I couldn’t put down. It is an extremely original and well thought out coming of age story: mild-mannered protagonists, charming would-be murderers, various miscreants which the hero takes under his wing. As the reader, you look back once you’re well into the story and see how everything ties together – It’s something I very much appreciate about Heyer’s works (or at least some of them). The story is absolutely hilarious at times as well. The romance is less developed than one might expect, but I really enjoyed the screen time between the hero and heroine. It was sweet and without conflict. The only thing I didn’t like was the benevolent treatment of the villains – the book ends as a farce, and that is the one part of the book I felt was a bit sloppy. But whatever, it’s a great adventure and a book that definitely has its moments. <br /><br />7/20/13<br />I think what I enjoyed most about Heyer's <em>The Foundling</em> is that it’s such an oddity. It’s a Regency novel that’s neither a romance nor a mystery. I suppose it’s somewhat a coming-of-age plot, but for the most part it’s simply a story of historical adventure. The irregularities don’t end there. The hero, Gilly, is the last man you would expect to be a young duke. He’s kind-hearted, conscientious, wants to marry for love, and is initially somewhat diffident. And yet - since he is one of Heyer’s creations – his character comes across as completely plausible. Gilly has been cosseted by well-meaning relatives and servants all his life, and is semi-serious when he wonders what it would be like to be a mere “mister.” So when the opportunity for adventure presents itself, he ventures off alone to prove to himself he’s more than just a duke. He runs into a great number of adventures along the way, from being kidnapped and arrested to taking on the exasperating burden of being a guardian to mischievous young man and a stunningly beautiful, yet brainless, young woman. It’s rather silly, and rather fun.<br /><br />There is a small romance subplot to the story – taking place over only a handful of the scenes – that is actually quite sweet. Gilly has known his love interest, Harriet, for most of his life, although they haven’t had much of a chance to get to know each other over the years. They have a longstanding agreement arranged by their parents. Gilly holds Harriet in great affection, but at the beginning of the story thinks what he feels isn’t quite love. As his adventures come to a close, however, he gets the opportunity to see what an understanding and competent woman Harriet is, and how he would be lucky to have such a woman for his duchess. For her part, Harriet comes off as an extremely sweet young woman… but perhaps a bit too submissive in her love of Gilly. With his newfound confidence, I would hate for him to run roughshod over her in any way.<br /><br />I gave <em>The Foundling</em> only four stars because there times when the plot becomes a borderline farce – e.g. when the villain exhibits the deductive prowess of Sherlock Holmes from the letter "S", when the hero’s servants gets into a tizzy over his disappearance, or when the hero rewards the man who had him kidnapped and would have had him murdered for enough money. That level of absurdity detracted from my enjoyment of the book. Overall, however, it was an entertaining story quite unlike anything I’ve read before.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5113429021549445102">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6933132933555315419">This is is my first Heyer read with a male protagonist as the dominant character, and I was a little worried that it would be entirely filled with gambling, races, boxing, and other manly pursuits, which I find completely boring. It was not, however - it was a delightful adventure and character study of a realistic and endearing young gentleman. I absolutely loved the character arc that Sale passes through. His growth is subtle, but the difference by the end is tremendous, and I loved seeing him</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6933132933555315419">This is is my first Heyer read with a male protagonist as the dominant character, and I was a little worried that it would be entirely filled with gambling, races, boxing, and other manly pursuits, which I find completely boring. It was not, however - it was a delightful adventure and character study of a realistic and endearing young gentleman. I absolutely loved the character arc that Sale passes through. His growth is subtle, but the difference by the end is tremendous, and I loved seeing him "come into his own," while still remaining his gentle, considerate self. My only complaints are that it is kind of slow, especially in the beginning, and that the title is totally lame.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17795716681705028693">I have a fondness for "Mr. Dash of Nowhere in Particular." Something about the description of the meek young duke, ruled over by his strong-willed, crotchety relations and servants spoke to me. I do think the romance in this book seemed like something of an afterthought, put in at the end only because Heyer's readers are used to seeing a pat happy ending. I didnt' think it needed it. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_74083518">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74083518" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/56479-res" class="left imgcol" title="Res"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1177127447p2/56479.jpg" alt="Res" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/74083518?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/56479-res" class="user" title="Res">Res</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/56479-res?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer74083518">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2565164895619491564">The one where, thanks to wealth, power, shortness, and a sickly childhood, Gilly isn't allowed to take a step without ten people attending him, until he breaks free and goes on an adventure of his own.<br /><br />As I mentioned in my notes on <a title="Sprig Muslin by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32107.Sprig_Muslin">Sprig Muslin</a>, these two books start off their adventures in pretty much the same way: a man, on his way to propose a marriage he isn't very enthusiastic about, finds himself saddled with a beautiful woman-child whose innocence he has to protect and a heedless schoolboy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2565164895619491564">The one where, thanks to wealth, power, shortness, and a sickly childhood, Gilly isn't allowed to take a step without ten people attending him, until he breaks free and goes on an adventure of his own.<br /><br />As I mentioned in my notes on <a title="Sprig Muslin by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32107.Sprig_Muslin">Sprig Muslin</a>, these two books start off their adventures in pretty much the same way: a man, on his way to propose a marriage he isn't very enthusiastic about, finds himself saddled with a beautiful woman-child whose innocence he has to protect and a heedless schoolboy who complicates things with his impulsiveness. <br /><br />The romance is better developed in Sprig Muslin. Here, though Harriet comes to the rescue courageously in the latter section of the book, she's really only a small part of Gilly's overall declaration of independence. <br /><br />I also prefer the girl-and-boy complications in Sprig Muslin; here, Tom is just annoying, and Belinda seems alarmingly simpleminded.<br /><br />What The Foundling has that Sprig Muslin lacks: First, Liversedge, the golden-tongued villain who always lands on his feet; second, Gilly coming into his own, which is the great pleasure of the book.<br /><br />Again, the same conclusion: read them both.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2565164895619491564">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/373336-mikki" class="user" title="Mikki">Mikki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/6414515-the-foundling" title="Paperback 9781402219481" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/373336-mikki?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/373336-mikki?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/373336-mikki?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer99152051">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17383155384845663832">To be honest, it was something of a chore to read this at first, but don't be deterred! Although it takes a while for the story to pick up and get interesting, the characters were charming enough to see me through the boring parts. I love that the protagonist isn't the typical swaggering, brooding hero of most Regency novels. Gilly makes you want to pinch him and gather him up in a hug, not swoon on your feet -- and that's a refreshing change.<br /><br />It's difficult not to enjoy Gilly's discovery of his</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17383155384845663832">To be honest, it was something of a chore to read this at first, but don't be deterred! Although it takes a while for the story to pick up and get interesting, the characters were charming enough to see me through the boring parts. I love that the protagonist isn't the typical swaggering, brooding hero of most Regency novels. Gilly makes you want to pinch him and gather him up in a hug, not swoon on your feet -- and that's a refreshing change.<br /><br />It's difficult not to enjoy Gilly's discovery of his capacity for independence as much as he does. The progression from naive lordling to a Duke (with the proper capitalization) completely pulled me in, and by the time he was properly Capitalized and master of himself, I found myself cheering on every little victory he came across.<br /><br />This was very much an unexpected Heyer favorite.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17383155384845663832">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer159779588">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15955850155871631030">One of the best Heyers, full of all the usual nonsense--put-upon dukes, mistaken motives, potentially ruined reputations, strangely lovable rascals, overbearing dowagers, humorous rustics, a beautiful girl without a brain in her head, and Hessian boots. Also coats with many capes. And curricles.<br /><br />I freakin' love Georgette Heyer. Many imitators, but only one of her.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1275014380">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11919937804161231372">I used to shy away from books with beautiful covers, thinking they must be sappy inside. <em>Anne of Green Gables</em> proved me wrong. <em>The Foundling</em> is another such gem, a Regency novel full of humor and adventure. A pleasant young Duke tries to do something by himself, for a change. But not selfishly--he keeps trying to help more people, with surprising results. Love blossoms, as well, but incidentally to the rest of the story. The characters have wonderfully distinct voices, and the Duke isn't the onl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11919937804161231372">I used to shy away from books with beautiful covers, thinking they must be sappy inside. <em>Anne of Green Gables</em> proved me wrong. <em>The Foundling</em> is another such gem, a Regency novel full of humor and adventure. A pleasant young Duke tries to do something by himself, for a change. But not selfishly--he keeps trying to help more people, with surprising results. Love blossoms, as well, but incidentally to the rest of the story. The characters have wonderfully distinct voices, and the Duke isn't the only one who grows up a little. I just loved this book!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11919937804161231372">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/40648422-samuraikitty?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40648422-samuraikitty?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1224730700">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4646309702194818196">I wouldn't necessarily call this Heyer novel a romance. There really isn't any. I haven't read "The Foundling" in years, and I mean years! Probably last read it in high school. What this story really is, is a coming of adulthood story about the Most Noble Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, Duke of Sale and Marquis of Ormesby; Earl of Sale; Baron Ware of Thame; Baron Ware of Stoven; and Baron Ware of Rufford. Or just Gilly to his family and friends. Gilly is 24 years old; he's been sickly most of hi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4646309702194818196">I wouldn't necessarily call this Heyer novel a romance. There really isn't any. I haven't read "The Foundling" in years, and I mean years! Probably last read it in high school. What this story really is, is a coming of adulthood story about the Most Noble Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, Duke of Sale and Marquis of Ormesby; Earl of Sale; Baron Ware of Thame; Baron Ware of Stoven; and Baron Ware of Rufford. Or just Gilly to his family and friends. Gilly is 24 years old; he's been sickly most of his life; he's short in stature, he's small - he is no ones idea of what a Duke should look like, or act like. He's coddled by his retainers and guardian, literally wrapped in lambs wool; and he's such a people pleaser that he doesn't push back to assert himself, even when all his well wishers frustrate him .... until one day he has had ENOUGH! And is given the opportunity to do something completely on his own to help his younger cousin out of a potentially scandalous situation. <br />The thing I love about Georgette Heyer's novels is this: If you want to know what the social history of Georgian and Regency life was like, by reading her novels you will learn while enjoying yourself. And not only about the Haute Ton - oh no - but about all levels of society. How people dressed, how they spoke, what they ate, what they drove, how they conducted themselves in their daily lives; the slang terms each level of society used, where they lived, etc. And the wit that Heyer used when writing her Regency and Georgian books: it's just awe inspiring! No one then (she started writing in the 20's) and no one now does the genre better in my opinion - no one.<br />This novel takes us jauntering about the countryside while Gilly gets himself into and out of adventures, and in the process learns a lot about himself and what he's capable of. Again, I would not call this a romance, but it's such a wonderful story, and the attention to detail is, as always with Heyer impeccable. I enjoyed it very much!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4646309702194818196">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10962779807178233874">The one where a young Duke is tired of being cosseted and decides to finally find out what life is like for plain Mr. Dash, of Nowhere in Particular.<br /><br />At 24, His Grace Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware (Gilly, to his friends) is sick of everyone treating him like a child. His uncle and his entire staff fear for his life if he so much as walks outside in the evenings, always terrified he might catch cold, because after all, he was such a sickly child. So when his young cousin is being blackmailed by t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10962779807178233874">The one where a young Duke is tired of being cosseted and decides to finally find out what life is like for plain Mr. Dash, of Nowhere in Particular.<br /><br />At 24, His Grace Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware (Gilly, to his friends) is sick of everyone treating him like a child. His uncle and his entire staff fear for his life if he so much as walks outside in the evenings, always terrified he might catch cold, because after all, he was such a sickly child. So when his young cousin is being blackmailed by the ward of a young girl he has fallen in love with, Gilly sees his opportunity to prove to everyone that he can take care of himself. On the way, he discovers that the woman his uncle deemed an appropriate future Duchess is actually the perfect girl for him, helps a young boy run away from his tutor (a most odious Mr. Snape), takes the young girl his cousin fell in love (the "Foundling" from the books' title) under his wing and helps her find the man she truly loves, gets kidnapped and held for ransom, is almost challenged to a duel, and gets himself into quite a number of other scrapes. <br /><br />I thought it was a lovely story. Gilly and Harriet are both perfectly average (not particularly handsome, or tall, or in any way extraordinary), and that's what makes them so loveable. They both have to figure out who they are and what they want, and it's just fun to see them getting themselves out of a lot of trouble and learning to stand up for themselves. The supporting characters (especially the villain, Mr. Liversedge) are also highly entertaining. All in all, I think it's not as delightful and funny as some of my favorite of Heyer's novels (like Venetia, Arabella, The Grand Sophy, or The Unknown Ajax), but still a highly enjoyable read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_667067494">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667067494" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="left imgcol" title="QNPoohBear"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1394921233p2/22177907.jpg" alt="QNPoohBear" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/667067494?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="user" title="QNPoohBear">QNPoohBear</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3537192-the-foundling" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=regency-romance" class="actionLinkLite">regency-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=kisses-only" class="actionLinkLite">kisses-only</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer667067494">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12740224217078226735"> The hero of this novel, the Most Noble Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, Duke of Sale and Marquis of Ormesby; Earl of Sale; Baron Ware of Thame; Baron Ware of Stoven; and Baron Ware of Rufford, a sickly orphan, was raised by a host of well-meaning relatives and old family retainers. He's been coddled and cosseted his whole life but now that he's on the verge of coming of full age, his uncle Lionel encourages him to make his own decisions, yet every time Gilly makes a move, he's told he should lis</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12740224217078226735"> The hero of this novel, the Most Noble Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, Duke of Sale and Marquis of Ormesby; Earl of Sale; Baron Ware of Thame; Baron Ware of Stoven; and Baron Ware of Rufford, a sickly orphan, was raised by a host of well-meaning relatives and old family retainers. He's been coddled and cosseted his whole life but now that he's on the verge of coming of full age, his uncle Lionel encourages him to make his own decisions, yet every time Gilly makes a move, he's told he should listen to his olders and betters, including the issue of marriage and Gilly is tired of it all. After doing his duty and proposing marriage to his shy neighbor, Gilly takes himself off to London to mope and complain to his big cousin Gideon. Gideon is sympathetic and encourages Gilly to "shake his leash" yet Gilly is afraid of hurting anyone's feelings and much too timid to break out on his own. When his younger cousin Matthew gets into a scrape, Gilly decides it's time to act like a man and disappears from London without telling anyone where he's going or what he's doing. When Gilly heads to the countryside to rout out the villain who is blackmailing his cousin, he finds an adventure he never dreamed of involving runaway schoolboys, a beautiful empty-headed foundling, kidnappers, blackmailers, would-be murderers and various other people Gilly has never encountered before. Meanwhile, rumors about Gilly's disappearance swirl around London and Gideon is considered the prime suspect! Refusing to divulge his cousin's secrets, yet discovering Gilly is in danger, Gideon races off to rescue his little cousin and learns that Gilly is more than capable of handling anything that comes his way. Gilly learns to stand up for himself and his friends and finally becomes a man.<br /><br />The plot of this book is a departure from Heyer's usual formula. It's a screwball comedy/coming-of-age story rather than a romance. It also features a hero who is neither a Corinthian or a Buck or a Beau and the hero's closest relatives do not desire his title! The story also centers solely around Gilly and doesn't enter into the mind of a heroine. The plot starts off slow and Gilly seems like an unappealing hero. He is rather boring and acquiesces to the wishes of his uncle far too easily. At first, Gideon seems like a better hero because he's tall and dashing with a crooked smile, but he's relegated to the background and this is only Gilly's story. There are some red herrings in the plot that depart from convention as well. I had a hard time getting into the story until about 3/4 of the way through when the adventure really began. Then I found myself engaged in the story, dying to find out what happened next and laughing out loud at Gilly's young protegee Tom and his destruction of Gilly's reputation. It seems like Heyer was poking fun at conventions and romance novels and created the antihero, anti-romance novel. It's not necessarily bad but I miss the charm and witty dialogue that is the hallmark of her romance novels. If you're looking for something different and well-written, give this a try, but don't expect convention.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12740224217078226735">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_75910116">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75910116" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1644165-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226207883p2/1644165.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/75910116?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 24, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1644165-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6414515-the-foundling" title="Paperback 9781402219481" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1644165-jessica?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer75910116">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer362680371444138340">Another lovely reading experience, brought to you by Georgette Heyer. I think that this one is my favorite so far by her. It had all of the components of her other historical romances, but this one managed to pull them all off flawlessly. It is a slightly different story than seems typical for her books, but maybe that's why I liked it so much.<br />The Duke of Sale, known as Gilly to most people (his full name and titles are amusingly very long), is an orphan, raised by his uncle until he reaches his</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText362680371444138340">Another lovely reading experience, brought to you by Georgette Heyer. I think that this one is my favorite so far by her. It had all of the components of her other historical romances, but this one managed to pull them all off flawlessly. It is a slightly different story than seems typical for her books, but maybe that's why I liked it so much.<br />The Duke of Sale, known as Gilly to most people (his full name and titles are amusingly very long), is an orphan, raised by his uncle until he reaches his majority at age 25. We meet him at 24, and see in him a man who has been so sheltered and cared for all of his life, that he practically cannot stand up for himself. He wants to speak for himself, and live his own life, but he knows that those responsible for his extreme disconnection from the world, his uncle and servants, only treat him so because they love him so much. And he does not have the heart to cause strife among his household. However, we see that this "mollycoddling" has begun to be simply too much for him, and he begins to show signs of breaking free. When his cousin finds himself in some trouble, Gilly volunteers to solve the problem. His first step? Tricking his servants and informing absolutely no one, not even his closest friend Gideon (another cousin), of his intentions, he sets out to have himself an adventure, to prove to himself whether he is "a man, or only a duke."<br />Gilly is a fantastic character, one whose strength the reader can see through all of the sheltering he has grown up with. The other male characters are equally well-drawn; I especially love Gideon, and his attitude towards Gilly, who he insists on calling Adolphus (his true first name). The two main female characters are also likeable, and Heyer does a terrific job of making us love the foundling Belinda, while being just as annoyed with her as the rest of the cast of characters most of the time. The romance in this book is more subtle than in the others, but I found it perhaps even more satisfying. Like I said, this is my favorite of the Heyer books I have read so far, and I would definitely recommend it to fans of historical fiction and romance. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="362680371444138340">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_136427086">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136427086" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/836085-asma" class="left imgcol" title="Asma"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1331274423p2/836085.jpg" alt="Asma" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/136427086?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/836085-asma" class="user" title="Asma">Asma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311122.The_Foundling" title="Paperback 9780099468066" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer136427086">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1334911401551577446">Orphaned at a young age, the Duke of Sale, or Gilly as everyone calls him, led a sheltered life thanks to his guardian and uncle, and the servants of his household. Nearing the age of when he'll handle complete control of his estate, he doubts his abilities to stand his ground against many who want his best interest. When he finds that his cousin is being blackmailed by Belinda, a mysterious beautiful girl, Gilly takes this opportunity to escape his stifling life and straighten the misunderstand</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1334911401551577446">Orphaned at a young age, the Duke of Sale, or Gilly as everyone calls him, led a sheltered life thanks to his guardian and uncle, and the servants of his household. Nearing the age of when he'll handle complete control of his estate, he doubts his abilities to stand his ground against many who want his best interest. When he finds that his cousin is being blackmailed by Belinda, a mysterious beautiful girl, Gilly takes this opportunity to escape his stifling life and straighten the misunderstanding. However, instead of a short and easy trip, the Duke is hurdled through complicated events and into the heart of adventure. <br /><br />I loved this book. I love it so much, I'm sad right now, because I'm leaving my crush behind (and no, it's not Gilly). Heyer is wonderful at building her characters and their environments, and this one is no different. Amazing, amazing characters, both the major and supportive ones. I wasn't convinced with Gilly as the main character because he lacked a bit of assertiveness, but his growth at the end of the book is admirable. The events itself are hilarious. Even when I was in a bad mood, Heyer managed to pull me into her story and crack me up with her characters. <br /><br />I wished there was a little more focus on the romance, but I was still satisfied with how things turned out. Amazing read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1334911401551577446">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer6984832099797910309">I'm rereading this delightful book for the umpteenth time now that I've discovered it at Audible in audiobook form.<br /><br />Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, the Duke of Sale, known as Gilly to his friends, is a mild-mannered and kind-hearted young man. He is too kind, in fact, to snub the well meaning servants and relatives who push him around "for his own good." When a chance for independence and adventure comes in the form of helping a young relative out of a fix, Gilly jumps at the chance to be "plain</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6984832099797910309">I'm rereading this delightful book for the umpteenth time now that I've discovered it at Audible in audiobook form.<br /><br />Adolphus Gillespie Vernon Ware, the Duke of Sale, known as Gilly to his friends, is a mild-mannered and kind-hearted young man. He is too kind, in fact, to snub the well meaning servants and relatives who push him around "for his own good." When a chance for independence and adventure comes in the form of helping a young relative out of a fix, Gilly jumps at the chance to be "plain Mr. Dash of Nowhere." Naturally he finds that there is a great deal of inconvenience in being poor and anonymous. However, in extricating himself from the series of adventures that ensue, he also finds himself and true love. <br /><br />Heyer's trademark humorous, charming romances are written for those of us who don't want bodice rippers and appreciate being credit for having a bit of intelligence. This one is a romance that actually doesn't dwell much on the romance and features a well-turned plot, a sense of the ridiculous, and a bit of escapism.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_49076507">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49076507" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1099250-kitaabi" class="left imgcol" title="Kitaabi"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350018868p2/1099250.jpg" alt="Kitaabi" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/49076507?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1099250-kitaabi" class="user" title="Kitaabi">Kitaabi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311122.The_Foundling" title="Paperback 9780099468066" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer49076507'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49076507">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13756108030124114852">The Duke of Sale (having had the misfortune of being a sickly child) has been cosseted &amp; coddled for all his life by his relatives and servants. Being 24 now and still having to endure advice and fussing and overprotectiveness meant that when the opportunity presented itself he gladly took the chance to slip his leash and try being a Dash of Nowhere in Particular. He decides that he will help out his cousin Matt from his troubles of being blackmailed by a scoudrel called Mr Liversedge and go</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13756108030124114852">The Duke of Sale (having had the misfortune of being a sickly child) has been cosseted &amp; coddled for all his life by his relatives and servants. Being 24 now and still having to endure advice and fussing and overprotectiveness meant that when the opportunity presented itself he gladly took the chance to slip his leash and try being a Dash of Nowhere in Particular. He decides that he will help out his cousin Matt from his troubles of being blackmailed by a scoudrel called Mr Liversedge and goes off leaving only his elder cousin Gideon (beloved because he seems to be the only fellow who doesn't adopt and fatherly, matronly or toadeating attitude with him) vaguely aware of his intentions of pursuing adventures.<br /><br />And adventures he does have! From wresting personal letters from Liversedge to getting saddled with an addlebrained beauty (who has a habit of running off with people who offer her purple, silk gowns and a ring), to rescuing a young charge running away from his home (who is determined to get up to all sorts of mischief like imitating highwaymen and getting locked up), to getting kidnapped by Liversedge. Never a dull moment for Mr Dash of Nowhere though it has to be said he acquits himself well. Meanwhile there is Gideon, who having known to be the last person the Duke saw before disappearing is being thought of as a murderer for his cousin's inheritance. To Gideon's credit he doesn't let such paltry rumours get in the way of his cousin's adventures but when Liversedge comes on his doorstep offering to kill his cousin for fifty thousand pounds even Gideon can't refrain from wanting to (after sufficiently strangling Liversedge) protect his "little one" and launches forth on a rescue mission which (he is happy to discover) wasn't needed at all, the Duke having burnt the place of his hostage to a cinder and made good his escape. <br /><br />The relationship between Gideon &amp; Gilly is absolutely adorable. Captain Ware believes in his young cousin's ability to take care of himself and manage his own affairs and while his father, who is uncle to Gilly, is forever contradicting himself by admonishing Gilly to assert himself and just when Gilly tries to do so waves them away as being silly or quite ineligible Gideon at least knows his cousin's strengths and is amused to witness his little one's transformation from being a quite and docile young man to someone who is firmly polite in refusing the various offers of help he is forever being showered with. This book also has one of Heyer's most amusing villains who while being such a scoundrel has so much sensibility (or so he is always saying) and such grand schemes that by the end Gilly and Gideon are inclined more to laugh at him and reward him for being such a villain than clap him in Newgate. Mr Liversedge asserts till the very end that had it not been for his various trickeries and villainy the Duke would never have had such adventures and found himself from someone who was unsure of himself to one who could come off creditably in all manner of deuced devlish situations. He almost convinces us too.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13756108030124114852">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48302543?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/105717-inbetween" class="user" title="_inbetween_">_inbetween_</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3195166-the-foundling" title="Paperback 9780749304485" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48302543">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17994132621487541556">Reading is only for the young.<br /><br />Gilly/Gideon<br /><br />I never wanted to read any Heyer slash. That should be self-explanatory, because her romances were the only real ones, with the m and f really belonging together, fitting, genuine love, affection and attraction, it made me sick to consider slashing the men, no matter how many there were, how many were attractive in every way. It still makes me sick. <br /><br />But Gideon's love for his "little one", and that first scene were Gilly comes a little bit apart and a lit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17994132621487541556">Reading is only for the young.<br /><br />Gilly/Gideon<br /><br />I never wanted to read any Heyer slash. That should be self-explanatory, because her romances were the only real ones, with the m and f really belonging together, fitting, genuine love, affection and attraction, it made me sick to consider slashing the men, no matter how many there were, how many were attractive in every way. It still makes me sick. <br /><br />But Gideon's love for his "little one", and that first scene were Gilly comes a little bit apart and a little bit into his own while looking up at his best friend, they even had me wonder if Gilly wasn't meant to be a woman in a romance about him and Gideon, with her adventuring, it would all fit - except the first chapters paint such an excellent picture of this sweet natured young man, and she's dead so I will never know. But scenes between men of various ages and brains tend to be her best, and the four novels I now reread emphasis that GH always wrote antiromance-<br /><br />but not like Beaton! Who is genuinely nasty and depressing, while reviled GH is more genuinely feminist and empowering and of course in another league, ten thousand miles above that hack, with her great talent in writing people and scenes and plots like clockwork, the elegance of it all evolving and fitting and making sense and amusing and formerly warming a dead-now girl's heart.<br /><br /><br />I also cannot understand why a critic said "all her heroines are young, beautiful and lively" when that is blatantly untrue, and why that is quoted now, on novels where those girls are witless antiheroines. Just like that phrase I remember from her biography, oddly the only one, that her daughter in law luckily was one of those golden girls Heyer used to write about, when those blonde beauties that dazzled and shone like gold were nearly always those the heroes or heroines had to take care of.<br /><br />I cannot post this, not even on GR, because GH is too ingrained in me and I cannot discuss her novels with people who find her boring or worse anyway, esp. when I criticise.<br /><br />And I loved Gilly. Even such pet names are different in GH - I never noticed them, and they are only given to people whom they suit by people who would. A Freddy, Ferdy or Gilly is not the same as a Hugh or Ivo, a Kitty is no Serena. Her novels also do not really change pov like that woman said - this is Gilly's book, and a romance about him, because you love him and know that she always loved him so it is a happy end.<br />And Gilly standing up to Gideon on that matter of Belinda not becoming a whore was one of those priceless little in-between moments, so important, even when I thought we heard often enough how Gilly changed, even when I didn't laugh at Tom. Or the minute he was tempted to leave her with his brother in law, human and real and making the rage following right after all the more gratifvying.<br /><br />Having read most of her books dozens of times, unlike any of my other adult novels, it is only now that I think - huh, at least five of them have exactly this theme, so maybe others share another theme. I always grouped them a little in my mind, and I think I reread those with so little couple interplay less, but I never EVER noticed the similarities, and it's a coincidence I reread them in this order now, more a following of the quieter guys - and all of them have a stunning blonde beauty of little brains and a tall dark dashing heartless cousin, and the quiet romance sort of confirmed at the end.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17994132621487541556">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1079189168">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer292354776290614228">I've been a Heyer fan ever since I read my first work by her, also the first romance novel in my 60 years of reading. Again, Heyer does not fail to deliver yet another charming and witty Regency era book. Usually she writs from the perspective of an independent woman of either noble or genteel birth. Here she gives a great account of an overly protected Duke who escapes his handlers to spend several harrowing, exciting and often dangerous days as "Mr. Dash of Nowhere In Particular". Great story!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer70475998">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5288785439624636579">This Heyer book isn't a "romance," per se--it's more of a coming-of-age story about a young, good-natured but over-protected Duke who slips away from the people caring for him and has a series of madcap adventures that teaches him to assert himself better. Gilly (Adolphus Gillespie) is an adorable main character: sweet and polite to a fault, empathic and kind, and it's fun to watch him get some self-esteem while not losing his better qualities. The romance part is slight but charming as well, as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5288785439624636579">This Heyer book isn't a "romance," per se--it's more of a coming-of-age story about a young, good-natured but over-protected Duke who slips away from the people caring for him and has a series of madcap adventures that teaches him to assert himself better. Gilly (Adolphus Gillespie) is an adorable main character: sweet and polite to a fault, empathic and kind, and it's fun to watch him get some self-esteem while not losing his better qualities. The romance part is slight but charming as well, as Gilly becomes more able to love his sweet childhood friend who he's been bullied into an engagement with, once he realizes who <em>he</em> is through his adventures. Gilly and Harry (short for Harriet) are shy introverts who eventually learn to be happy together and create a bond of shared feeling that's very endearing.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5288785439624636579">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CVTOsPCRWC32qQ+UIZ1fmBor1B2/c1JayMKHyxMyOg1sgPFjAkNM13pxey9f/LkqU9wXBPauFfCiy4JZ36fMSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9352420532885187435">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9352420532885187435">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9352420532885187435">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Georgette Heyer...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
